# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`

# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Implementation

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement RBAC authorization. Identify: the RBACAuthorizer with its Authorize method (in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/), the SubjectAccessEvaluator, the DefaultRuleResolver that resolves PolicyRules for a user, the SubjectAccessReview REST handler, the bootstrap RBAC policy definitions, and the policy-based storage for Role and ClusterRoleBinding objects with escalation prevention.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive documentation of the Kubernetes RBAC authorization implementation, including:

### **24 Key Source Files** covering:

1. **Core Authorization Engine** (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go)
   - RBACAuthorizer with Authorize method
   - RequestToRuleMapper interface
   - RuleAllows function for permission checking

2. **Subject Access Evaluator** (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go)
   - SubjectAccessEvaluator for resolving subjects that can perform actions

3. **Policy Rule Resolution** (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go)
   - DefaultRuleResolver implementing AuthorizationRuleResolver
   - VisitRulesFor and RulesFor methods
   - GetRoleReferenceRules for resolving role bindings

4. **SubjectAccessReview REST Handlers** (4 files under pkg/registry/authorization/)
   - SubjectAccessReview, LocalSubjectAccessReview
   - SelfSubjectAccessReview, SelfSubjectRulesReview

5. **Bootstrap RBAC Policies** (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/)
   - Default cluster roles and bindings
   - Controller-specific policies
   - Namespace-scoped defaults

6. **Escalation Prevention** (pkg/registry/rbac/)
   - escalation_check.go: EscalationAllowed, RoleEscalationAuthorized, BindingAuthorized
   - Policy-based storage for Role, ClusterRole, RoleBinding, ClusterRoleBinding
   - ConfirmNoEscalation validation in validation/ package

interconnected packages in kubernetes/kubernetes:\\n\\n## Core Authorization Engine\\n\\nThe primary RBAC authorization logic is located in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go. The RBACAuthorizer struct implements the authorizer.Authorizer interface and contains an Authorize method that evaluates authorization requests. The Authorize method uses a RequestToRuleMapper interface to resolve policy rules for a given user. The authorization flow uses an authorizingVisitor pattern that short-circuits on first match, checking each applicable rule using the RuleAllows function which matches verbs, API groups, resources, and resource names against the request attributes.\\n\\n## Subject Access Evaluator\\n\\nThe SubjectAccessEvaluator is defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go and implements the SubjectLocator interface. Key methods include:\\n- RulesFor: Returns all applicable rules for a user in a namespace\\n- VisitRulesFor: Iterates through all applicable rules using a visitor pattern\\n- GetRoleReferenceRules: Resolves rules referenced by RoleBinding or ClusterRoleBinding objects\\n\\nThe DefaultRuleResolver works by examining ClusterRoleBindings and RoleBindings to find those that apply to the user (based on user name, group membership, or service account), then retrieving the actual PolicyRules from the referenced Role or ClusterRole objects.\\n\\n## SubjectAccessReview REST Handlers\\n\\nFour REST handlers are implemented for different SubjectAccessReview APIs:\\n1. pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go - Cluster-wide SubjectAccessReview\\n2. pkg/registry/authorization/localsubjectaccessreview/rest.go - Namespace-scoped LocalSubjectAccessReview\\n3. pkg/registry/authorization/selfsubjectaccessreview/rest.go - Self-check SelfSubjectAccessReview\\n4. pkg/registry/authorization/selfsubjectrulesreview/rest.go - Rule enumeration SelfSubjectRulesReview\\n\\nThese REST handlers are registered via the RESTStorageProvider in pkg/registry/authorization/rest/storage_authorization.go.\\n\\n## Bootstrap RBAC Policies\\n\\nDefault RBAC policies are defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/:\\n- policy.go: Main bootstrap policies defining default roles and bindings\\n- controller_policy.go: Policies for built-in controllers\\n- namespace_policy.go: Namespace-scoped default roles\\n\\n## Escalation Prevention\\n\\nThe system prevents privilege escalation through several mechanisms:\\n\\n1. pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go contains:\\n   - EscalationAllowed: Checks if user is in the system:masters group\\n   - RoleEscalationAuthorized: Checks if user is explicitly authorized to escalate role permissions\\n   - BindingAuthorized: Checks if user is authorized to bind a specific role\\n\\n2. interconnected packages in kubernetes/kubernetes:\\n\\n## Core Authorization Engine\\n\\nThe primary RBAC authorization logic is located in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go. The RBACAuthorizer struct implements the authorizer.Authorizer interface and contains an Authorize method that evaluates authorization requests. The Authorize method uses a RequestToRuleMapper interface to resolve policy rules for a given user. The authorization flow uses an authorizingVisitor pattern that short-circuits on first match, checking each applicable rule using the RuleAllows function which matches verbs, API groups, resources, and resource names against the request attributes.\\n\\n## Subject Access Evaluator\\n\\nThe SubjectAccessEvaluator is defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go and implements the SubjectLocator interface. It resolves all subjects that can perform a specific action using the RoleToRuleMapper interface to determine which roles are applicable to different users and groups.\\n\\n## Policy Rule Resolution - DefaultRuleResolver\\n\\nThe pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go file contains the DefaultRuleResolver, which implements the AuthorizationRuleResolver interface and is responsible for resolving PolicyRules for users. Key methods include:\\n- RulesFor: Returns all applicable rules for a user in a namespace\\n- VisitRulesFor: Iterates through all applicable rules using a visitor pattern\\n- GetRoleReferenceRules: Resolves rules referenced by RoleBinding or ClusterRoleBinding objects\\n\\nThe DefaultRuleResolver works by examining ClusterRoleBindings and RoleBindings to find those that apply to the user (based on user name, group membership, or service account), then retrieving the actual PolicyRules from the referenced Role or ClusterRole objects.\\n\\n## SubjectAccessReview REST Handlers\\n\\nFour REST handlers are implemented for different SubjectAccessReview APIs:\\n1. pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go - Cluster-wide SubjectAccessReview\\n2. pkg/registry/authorization/localsubjectaccessreview/rest.go - Namespace-scoped LocalSubjectAccessReview\\n3. pkg/registry/authorization/selfsubjectaccessreview/rest.go - Self-check SelfSubjectAccessReview\\n4. pkg/registry/authorization/selfsubjectrulesreview/rest.go - Rule enumeration SelfSubjectRulesReview\\n\\nThese REST handlers are registered via the RESTStorageProvider in pkg/registry/authorization/rest/storage_authorization.go.\\n\\n## Bootstrap RBAC Policies\\n\\nDefault RBAC policies are defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/:\\n- policy.go: Main bootstrap policies defining default roles and bindings\\n- controller_policy.go: Policies for built-in controllers\\n- namespace_policy.go: Namespace-scoped default roles\\n\\n## Escalation Prevention\\n\\nThe system prevents privilege escalation through several mechanisms:\\n\\n1. pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go contains:\\n   - EscalationAllowed: Checks if user is in the system:masters group\\n   - RoleEscalationAuthorized: Checks if user is explicitly authorized to escalate role permissions\\n   - BindingAuthorized: Checks if user is authorized to bind a specific role\\n\\n2. Policy-based storage implementations enforce escalation checks:\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go\\n   - pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go\\n\\n3. Escalation validation via pkg/registry/rbac/validation/:\\n   - rule.go: ConfirmNoEscalation function ensures users cannot grant permissions they don't have\\n   - internal_version_adapter.go: ConfirmNoEscalationInternal converts between API versions\\n   - policy_compact.go: CompactRules optimizes rule comparison for escalation checks\\n\\n## Supporting Infrastructure\\n\\n- pkg/registry/rbac/helpers.go: Utility functions for RBAC object handling\\n- pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go: Main RBAC storage provider that wires all components together\\n- Storage implementations in pkg/registry/rbac/{role,clusterrole,rolebinding,clusterrolebinding}/storage/ and policybased/ directories\\n\\nThe entire system works together to provide a deny-by-default authorization model where rules are purely additive and users can only perform actions they have explicit permission for.\"\n}\n",
